<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Great Britain</h1> <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div> <div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">This article is about the island. For the state of which it is a part, see <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>. For the historical state, see <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Kingdom of Great Britain</a>. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Great_Britain_(disambiguation)" title="Great Britain (disambiguation)">Great Britain (disambiguation)</a> and <a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Britain_(disambiguation)" title="Britain (disambiguation)">Britain (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<p><b>Great Britain</b> is an <a href="/wiki/Island" title="Island">island</a> in the North <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> off the northwest coast of <a href="/wiki/Continental_Europe" title="Continental Europe">continental Europe</a>. With an area of 209,331 km<sup>2</sup> (80,823 sq mi), it is the largest of the <a href="/wiki/British_Isles" title="British Isles">British Isles</a>, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_European_islands_by_area" title="List of European islands by area">largest European island</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_by_area" title="List of islands by area">ninth-largest island in the world</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[note 1]</a></sup> In 2011, Great Britain had a population of about 61 million people, making it the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_by_population" title="List of islands by population">third-most populous island</a> after <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a> in Indonesia and <a href="/wiki/Honshu" title="Honshu">Honshu</a> in <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ons_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-ons-9">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[9]</a></sup> The island of <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a> is situated to the west of Great Britain, and together these islands, along with over <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_the_British_Isles" title="List of islands of the British Isles">1,000 smaller surrounding islands</a>, form the British Isles <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup>
</p><p>The island is dominated by a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maritime_climate" title="Maritime climate">maritime climate</a> with quite narrow temperature differences between seasons. Politically, Great Britain is part of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland</a>, and constitutes most of its territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oliver2003_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Oliver2003-12">[11]</a></sup> Most of <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a> are on the island.  The term "Great Britain" is often used to include the whole of England, Scotland and Wales including their component adjoining islands; and is also occasionally but contentiously applied to the UK as a whole in some contexts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup>
</p><p>A single <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Kingdom of Great Britain</a> resulted from the union of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">Kingdom of England</a> (which had already comprised the present-day countries of England and Wales) and the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Scotland" title="Kingdom of Scotland">Kingdom of Scotland</a> by the 1707 <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Union_1707" title="Acts of Union 1707">Acts of Union</a>. More than a hundred years before, in 1603, <a href="/wiki/James_VI_and_I" title="James VI and I">King James VI</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Scottish_monarchs" title="List of Scottish monarchs">King of Scots</a>, had inherited the throne of England, but it was not until 1707 that the two countries' parliaments agreed to form a political union. In 1801, Great Britain <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Union_1800" title="Acts of Union 1800">united</a> with the neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Ireland" title="Kingdom of Ireland">Kingdom of Ireland</a>, forming the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland</a>, which was renamed the "United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland" after the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Free_State" title="Irish Free State">Irish Free State</a> seceded in 1922.
</p>

</ul>
</li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminology">Terminology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Britain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Terminology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Terminology_of_the_British_Isles" title="Terminology of the British Isles">Terminology of the British Isles</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Toponymy">Toponymy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Britain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Toponymy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Britain_(place_name)" title="Britain (place name)">Britain (place name)</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> has been referred to by a single name for over 2000 years: the term '<a href="/wiki/British_Isles" title="British Isles">British Isles</a>' derives from terms used by classical geographers to describe this island group. By 50 BC Greek geographers were using equivalents of <i>Prettanikē</i> as a collective name for the British Isles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup> However, with the <a href="/wiki/Roman_conquest_of_Britain" title="Roman conquest of Britain">Roman conquest of Britain</a> the Latin term <i><a href="/wiki/Britannia" title="Britannia">Britannia</a></i> was used for the island of Great Britain, and later <a href="/wiki/Roman_Britain" title="Roman Britain">Roman-occupied Britain</a> south of <a href="/wiki/Caledonia" title="Caledonia">Caledonia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sax1_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-sax1-17">[16]</a></sup>
</p><p>The earliest known name for Great Britain is <i><a href="/wiki/Albion" title="Albion">Albion</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el">Ἀλβιών</span>) or <i>insula Albionum</i>, from either the Latin <i>albus</i> meaning "white" (possibly referring to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_cliffs_of_Dover" title="White cliffs of Dover">white cliffs of Dover</a>, the first view of Britain from the continent) or the "island of the <i>Albiones</i>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-snyder_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-snyder-18">[17]</a></sup>
</p><p>The oldest mention of terms related to Great Britain was by <a href="/wiki/Aristotle" title="Aristotle">Aristotle</a> (384–322 BC), or possibly by <a href="/wiki/Pseudo-Aristotle" title="Pseudo-Aristotle">Pseudo-Aristotle</a>, in his text <i><a href="/wiki/On_the_Universe" title="On the Universe">On the Universe</a></i>, Vol. III. To quote his works, "There are two very large islands in it, called the British Isles, Albion and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ierne_(placename)" title="Ierne (placename)">Ierne</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Pliny_the_Elder" title="Pliny the Elder">Pliny the Elder</a> (AD 23–79) in his <i><a href="/wiki/Natural_History_(Pliny)" title="Natural History (Pliny)">Natural History</a></i> records of Great Britain: "Its former name was Albion; but at a later period, all the islands, of which we shall just now briefly make mention, were included under the name of 'Britanniæ.'"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PlinyE(4.41)_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-PlinyE(4.41)-20">[19]</a></sup>
</p><p>The name <i>Britain</i> descends from the Latin name for Britain, <i>Britannia</i> or <i>Brittānia</i>, the land of the Britons. <a href="/wiki/Old_French" title="Old French">Old French</a> <i>Bretaigne</i> (whence also <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Modern_French" title="Modern French">Modern French</a> <i>Bretagne</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Middle_English" title="Middle English">Middle English</a> <i>Bretayne</i>, <i>Breteyne</i>. The French form replaced the <a href="/wiki/Old_English" title="Old English">Old English</a> <i>Breoton, Breoten, Bryten, Breten</i> (also <i>Breoton-lond, Breten-lond</i>). Britannia was used by the Romans from the 1st century BC for the British Isles taken together. It is derived from the travel writings of the Pytheas around 320 BC, which described various islands in the North Atlantic as far north as <a href="/wiki/Thule" title="Thule">Thule</a> (probably <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>).
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Marcian_of_Heraclea" title="Marcian of Heraclea">Marcian of Heraclea</a>, in his <i>Periplus maris exteri</i>, described the island group as <span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">αἱ Πρεττανικαὶ νῆσοι</span> (the Prettanic Isles).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MarcianPeriplus_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-MarcianPeriplus-21">[20]</a></sup>
</p><p>The peoples of these islands of <i>Prettanike</i> were called the Πρεττανοί, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Priteni" title="Priteni">Priteni</a></i> or <i>Pretani</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-snyder_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-snyder-18">[17]</a></sup>
<i>Priteni</i> is the source of the <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh language</a> term <a href="/wiki/Prydain" title="Prydain">Prydain</a>, <i>Britain</i>, which has the same source as the <a href="/wiki/Goidelic_languages" title="Goidelic languages">Goidelic</a> term <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cruithne_(people)" title="Cruithne (people)">Cruithne</a> used to refer to the early <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brythonic_languages" title="Brythonic languages">Brythonic</a>-speaking inhabitants of Ireland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup> The latter were later called <a href="/wiki/Picts" title="Picts">Picts</a> or <a href="/wiki/Caledonians" title="Caledonians">Caledonians</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a>. Greek historians <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diodorus_of_Sicily" title="Diodorus of Sicily">Diodorus of Sicily</a> and <a href="/wiki/Strabo" title="Strabo">Strabo</a> preserved variants of <i>Prettanike</i> from the work of Greek explorer <a href="/wiki/Pytheas" title="Pytheas">Pytheas</a> of <a href="/wiki/Marseille" title="Marseille">Massalia</a>, who travelled from his home in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hellenistic" title="Hellenistic">Hellenistic</a> southern <a href="/wiki/Gaul" title="Gaul">Gaul</a> to Britain in the 4th century BC. The term used by Pytheas may derive from a Celtic word meaning "the painted ones" or "the tattooed folk" in reference to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Woad" title="Woad">body decorations</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Derivation_of_Great">Derivation of <i>Great</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Britain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Derivation of Great">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Greeks_in_Egypt" title="Greeks in Egypt">Greco-Egyptian</a> scientist <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy" title="Ptolemy">Ptolemy</a> referred to the larger island as <i>great Britain</i> (μεγάλη Βρεττανία <i>megale Brettania</i>) and to Ireland as <i>little Britain</i> (μικρὰ Βρεττανία <i>mikra Brettania</i>) in his work <i><a href="/wiki/Almagest" title="Almagest">Almagest</a></i> (147–148 AD).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> In his later work, <i><a href="/wiki/Geography_(Ptolemy)" title="Geography (Ptolemy)">Geography</a></i> (c. 150 AD), he gave the islands the names <i><a href="/wiki/Albion" title="Albion">Alwion</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Hibernia" title="Hibernia">Iwernia</a></i>, and <i>Mona</i> (the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup> suggesting these may have been the names of the individual islands not known to him at the time of writing <i>Almagest</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup> The name <i>Albion</i> appears to have fallen out of use sometime after the <a href="/wiki/Roman_conquest_of_Britain" title="Roman conquest of Britain">Roman conquest of Britain</a>, after which <i>Britain</i> became the more commonplace name for the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-snyder_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-snyder-18">[17]</a></sup>
</p><p>After the Anglo-Saxon period, <i>Britain</i> was used as a historical term only.
<a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_of_Monmouth" title="Geoffrey of Monmouth">Geoffrey of Monmouth</a> in his <a href="/wiki/Pseudohistory" title="Pseudohistory">pseudohistorical</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Historia_Regum_Britanniae" title="Historia Regum Britanniae">Historia Regum Britanniae</a></i> (<i>c.</i> 1136) refers to the island as <i>Britannia major</i> ("Greater Britain"), to distinguish it from <i>Britannia minor</i> ("Lesser Britain"), the continental region which approximates to modern <a href="/wiki/Brittany" title="Brittany">Brittany</a>, which had been settled in the fifth and sixth centuries by migrants from Britain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup> The term <i>Great Britain</i> was first used officially in 1474, in the instrument drawing up the proposal for a marriage between <a href="/wiki/Cecily_of_York" title="Cecily of York">Cecily</a> the daughter of <a href="/wiki/Edward_IV_of_England" title="Edward IV of England">Edward IV of England</a>, and <a href="/wiki/James_IV_of_Scotland" title="James IV of Scotland">James</a> the son of <a href="/wiki/James_III_of_Scotland" title="James III of Scotland">James III of Scotland</a>, which described it as "this Nobill Isle, callit Gret Britanee". It was used again in 1604, when <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_I_of_England" title="James I of England">King James VI and I</a> styled himself "King of Great Brittaine, France and Ireland".
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_use_of_the_term_Great_Britain">Modern use of the term <i>Great Britain</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Britain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Modern use of the term Great Britain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Great Britain</i> refers geographically to the island of Great Britain. It is also often used to refer politically to the whole of <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a>, including their smaller off shore islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup> While it is sometimes used to refer to the whole of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, including Northern Ireland, this is not correct.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oed_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-oed-29">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brock_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-brock-30">[29]</a></sup>
</p><p>Similarly, <i><a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Britain_(disambiguation)" title="Britain (disambiguation)">Britain</a></i> can refer to either all islands in Great Britain, the largest island, or the political grouping of countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup> There is no clear distinction, even in government documents: the UK government yearbooks have used both <i>Britain</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup> and <i>United Kingdom</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup>
</p><p><i>GB</i> and <i>GBR</i> are used instead of <i>UK</i> in some international codes to refer to the United Kingdom, including the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Postal_Union" title="Universal Postal Union">Universal Postal Union</a>, international sports teams, <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Organization_for_Standardization" title="International Organization for Standardization">International Organization for Standardization</a> country codes <a href="/wiki/ISO_3166-2:GB" title="ISO 3166-2:GB">ISO 3166-2</a> and <a href="/wiki/ISO_3166-1_alpha-3" title="ISO 3166-1 alpha-3">ISO 3166-1 alpha-3</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_international_license_plate_codes" title="List of international license plate codes">international licence plate codes</a>.
</p><p>On the Internet, <a href="/wiki/.uk" title=".uk">.uk</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Country_code_top-level_domain" title="Country code top-level domain">country code top-level domain</a> for the United Kingdom. A <a href="/wiki/.gb" title=".gb">.gb</a> top-level domain was used to a limited extent, but is now obsolete because the domain name registrar will not take new registrations.
</p><p>In the Olympics, <i><a href="/wiki/Team_GB" title="Team GB">Team GB</a></i> is used by the <a href="/wiki/British_Olympic_Association" title="British Olympic Association">British Olympic Association</a> to represent the <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_at_the_Olympics" title="Great Britain at the Olympics">British Olympic team</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olympic_Council_of_Ireland" title="Olympic Council of Ireland">Olympic Council of Ireland</a> claims to represent the whole <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">island of Ireland</a>, and Northern Irish sportspeople may choose to compete for either team,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup> most choosing to represent Ireland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_definition">Political definition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Britain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Political definition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:England,_Scotland_and_Wales_within_the_UK_and_Europe.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="520" data-file-width="680" decoding="async" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/England%2C_Scotland_and_Wales_within_the_UK_and_Europe.svg/220px-England%2C_Scotland_and_Wales_within_the_UK_and_Europe.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/England%2C_Scotland_and_Wales_within_the_UK_and_Europe.svg/330px-England%2C_Scotland_and_Wales_within_the_UK_and_Europe.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/England%2C_Scotland_and_Wales_within_the_UK_and_Europe.svg/440px-England%2C_Scotland_and_Wales_within_the_UK_and_Europe.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:England,_Scotland_and_Wales_within_the_UK_and_Europe.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><div style="font-size:11px"><center>Political definition of Great Britain (<small>dark green</small>)</center></div><div style="font-size:11px"> – in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> (<small>green &amp; dark grey</small>)</div><div style="font-size:11px"> – in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> (<small>green</small>)</div></div></div></div>
<p>Politically, Great Britain refers to the whole of England, Scotland and Wales in combination,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Key_facts_about_the_United_Kingdom_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Key_facts_about_the_United_Kingdom-36">[35]</a></sup> but not <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>; it includes islands, such as the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Wight" title="Isle of Wight">Isle of Wight</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anglesey" title="Anglesey">Anglesey</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Isles_of_Scilly" title="Isles of Scilly">Isles of Scilly</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hebrides" title="Hebrides">Hebrides</a> and the island groups of <a href="/wiki/Orkney" title="Orkney">Orkney</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shetland" title="Shetland">Shetland</a>, that are part of England, Wales, or Scotland. It does not include the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Islands" title="Channel Islands">Channel Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Key_facts_about_the_United_Kingdom_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-Key_facts_about_the_United_Kingdom-36">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup>
</p><p>The political union that joined the kingdoms of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">England</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Scotland" title="Kingdom of Scotland">Scotland</a> happened in 1707 when the <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Union_1707" title="Acts of Union 1707">Acts of Union</a> ratified the 1706 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Union" title="Treaty of Union">Treaty of Union</a> and merged the parliaments of the two nations, forming the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Kingdom of Great Britain</a>, which covered the entire island. Before this, a personal union had existed between these two countries since the 1603 <a href="/wiki/Union_of_the_Crowns" title="Union of the Crowns">Union of the Crowns</a> under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_VI_of_Scotland_and_I_of_England" title="James VI of Scotland and I of England">James VI of Scotland and I of England</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Britain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistoric_period">Prehistoric period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Britain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Prehistoric period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Prehistoric_Britain" title="Prehistoric Britain">Prehistoric Britain</a></div>
<p>Great Britain was probably first inhabited by those who crossed on the land bridge from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_mainland" title="European mainland">European mainland</a>. <a href="/wiki/Happisburgh_footprints" title="Happisburgh footprints">Human footprints</a> have been found from over 800,000 years ago in <a href="/wiki/Norfolk" title="Norfolk">Norfolk</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc-2014-02-07_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-2014-02-07-38">[37]</a></sup> and traces of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Early_humans" title="Early humans">early humans</a> have been found (at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boxgrove_Quarry" title="Boxgrove Quarry">Boxgrove Quarry</a>, Sussex) from some 500,000 years ago<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Modern_humans" title="Modern humans">modern humans</a> from about 30,000 years ago. Until about 14,000 years ago, it was connected to <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>, and as recently as 8,000 years ago it retained a land connection to the continent, with <a href="/wiki/Doggerland" title="Doggerland">an area of mostly low marshland</a> joining it to what are now <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-drowning_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-drowning-40">[39]</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Cheddar_Gorge" title="Cheddar Gorge">Cheddar Gorge</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a>, the remains of animal species native to mainland Europe such as <a href="/wiki/Antelope" title="Antelope">antelopes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brown_bear" title="Brown bear">brown bears</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wild_horse" title="Wild horse">wild horses</a> have been found alongside a human skeleton, '<a href="/wiki/Cheddar_Man" title="Cheddar Man">Cheddar Man</a>', dated to about 7150 BC. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup> Great Britain became an island at the end of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Last_glacial_period" title="Last glacial period">last glacial period</a> when sea levels rose due to the combination of melting <a href="/wiki/Glacier" title="Glacier">glaciers</a> and the subsequent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isostatic_rebound" title="Isostatic rebound">isostatic rebound</a> of the crust.
Great Britain's <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a> inhabitants are known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Britons_(historic)" title="Britons (historic)">Britons</a>; they spoke <a href="/wiki/Celtic_languages" title="Celtic languages">Celtic languages</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roman_and_medieval_period">Roman and medieval period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Britain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Roman and medieval period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Roman_Britain" title="Roman Britain">Roman Britain</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medieval_England" title="Medieval England">Medieval England</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medieval_Scotland" title="Medieval Scotland">Medieval Scotland</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medieval_Wales" title="Medieval Wales">Medieval Wales</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Prima_Europe_tabula.jpg"><img alt="Ptolomy's historical map of Roman Britain" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4293" data-file-width="6000" decoding="async" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Prima_Europe_tabula.jpg/220px-Prima_Europe_tabula.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Prima_Europe_tabula.jpg/330px-Prima_Europe_tabula.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Prima_Europe_tabula.jpg/440px-Prima_Europe_tabula.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Prima_Europe_tabula.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Prima Europe tabula</i>. A copy of <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy" title="Ptolemy">Ptolemy</a>'s 2nd century map of Roman Britain</div></div></div>
<p>The Romans conquered most of the island (up to <a href="/wiki/Hadrian%27s_Wall" title="Hadrian's Wall">Hadrian's Wall</a> in northern England) and this became the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Ancient Roman</a> province of <i><a href="/wiki/Roman_Britain" title="Roman Britain">Britannia</a></i>. In the course of the 500 years after the Roman Empire fell, the Britons of the south and east of the island were assimilated or displaced by <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxon_settlement_of_Britain" title="Anglo-Saxon settlement of Britain">invading</a> <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic</a> tribes (<a href="/wiki/Angles" title="Angles">Angles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saxons" title="Saxons">Saxons</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jutes" title="Jutes">Jutes</a>, often referred to collectively as <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxons" title="Anglo-Saxons">Anglo-Saxons</a>). At about the same time, <a href="/wiki/Gaelic_Ireland" title="Gaelic Ireland">Gaelic</a> tribes from Ireland invaded the north-west, absorbing both the <a href="/wiki/Picts" title="Picts">Picts</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Britons_(historical)" title="Britons (historical)">Britons</a> of northern Britain, eventually forming the Kingdom of Scotland in the 9th century. The south-east of Scotland was colonised by the Angles and formed, until 1018, a part of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Northumbria" title="Kingdom of Northumbria">Kingdom of Northumbria</a>. Ultimately, the population of south-east Britain came to be referred to as the <a href="/wiki/English_people" title="English people">English people</a>, so-named after the Angles.
</p><p>Germanic speakers referred to Britons as <i>Welsh</i>. This term came to be applied exclusively to the inhabitants of what is now Wales, but it also survives in names such as <a href="/wiki/Wallace_(surname)" title="Wallace (surname)">Wallace</a> and in the second syllable of <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a>. <i>Cymry</i>, a name the Britons used to describe themselves, is similarly restricted in modern Welsh to people from Wales, but also survives in English in the place name of <a href="/wiki/Cumbria" title="Cumbria">Cumbria</a>. The Britons living in the areas now known as Wales, Cumbria and Cornwall were not assimilated by the Germanic tribes, a fact reflected in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Celtic_language-death_in_England" title="Celtic language-death in England">survival of Celtic languages</a> in these areas into more recent times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ellis1974_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ellis1974-42">[41]</a></sup> At the time of the Germanic invasion of Southern Britain, many Britons emigrated to the area now known as <a href="/wiki/Brittany" title="Brittany">Brittany</a>, where <a href="/wiki/Breton_language" title="Breton language">Breton</a>, a Celtic language closely related to Welsh and <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a> and descended from the language of the emigrants, is still spoken. In the 9th century, a series of Danish assaults on northern English kingdoms led to them coming under Danish control (an area known as the <a href="/wiki/Danelaw" title="Danelaw">Danelaw</a>). In the 10th century, however, all the English kingdoms were unified under one ruler as the kingdom of England when the last constituent kingdom, Northumbria, submitted to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Edgar_I" title="Edgar I">Edgar</a> in 959. In 1066, England was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norman_Conquest" title="Norman Conquest">conquered by the Normans</a>, who introduced a <a href="/wiki/Norman_language" title="Norman language">Norman</a>-speaking administration that was eventually assimilated. Wales came under Anglo-Norman control in 1282, and was officially annexed to England in the 16th century.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_modern_period">Early modern period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Britain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Early modern period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Early_modern_Britain" title="Early modern Britain">Early modern Britain</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="History of the United Kingdom">History of the United Kingdom</a></div>
<p>On 20 October 1604 <a href="/wiki/James_VI_and_I" title="James VI and I">King James</a>, who had succeeded separately to the two thrones of England and Scotland, proclaimed himself "King of Great Brittaine, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, and Ireland".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup> When James died in 1625 and the <a href="/wiki/Privy_Council_of_England" title="Privy Council of England">Privy Council of England</a> was drafting the proclamation of the new king, Charles I, a Scottish peer, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Erskine,_1st_Earl_of_Kellie" title="Thomas Erskine, 1st Earl of Kellie">Thomas Erskine, 1st Earl of Kellie</a>, succeeded in insisting that it use the phrase "King of Great Britain", which James had preferred, rather than King of Scotland and England (or vice versa).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup> While that title was also used by some of James's successors, England and Scotland each remained legally separate countries, each with its own parliament, until 1707, when each parliament passed an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Act_of_Union_1707" title="Act of Union 1707">Act of Union</a> to ratify the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Union" title="Treaty of Union">Treaty of Union</a> that had been agreed the previous year. This created a single kingdom out of two, with a single parliament, with effect from 1 May 1707. The Treaty of Union specified the name of the new all-island state as "Great Britain", while describing it as "One Kingdom" and "the United Kingdom". To most historians, therefore, the all-island state that existed between 1707 and 1800 is "Great Britain" or the "Kingdom of Great Britain".
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Britain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_England" title="Geography of England">Geography of England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Scotland" title="Geography of Scotland">Geography of Scotland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Wales" title="Geography of Wales">Geography of Wales</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Geography of the United Kingdom">Geography of the United Kingdom</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:France_manche_vue_dover.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="258" data-file-width="593" decoding="async" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/France_manche_vue_dover.JPG/300px-France_manche_vue_dover.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/France_manche_vue_dover.JPG/450px-France_manche_vue_dover.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/27/France_manche_vue_dover.JPG 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:France_manche_vue_dover.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View of Britain's coast from northern France</div></div></div>
<p>Great Britain lies on the European continental shelf, part of the <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Plate" title="Eurasian Plate">Eurasian Plate</a>. Situated off the north-west coast of <a href="/wiki/Continental_Europe" title="Continental Europe">continental Europe</a>, it is separated from the mainland by the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a> and by the <a href="/wiki/English_Channel" title="English Channel">English Channel</a>, which narrows to 34 km (18 nmi; 21 mi) at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Straits_of_Dover" title="Straits of Dover">Straits of Dover</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup> It stretches over about ten degrees of <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">latitude</a> on its longer, north-south axis and occupies an area of 209,331 km<sup>2</sup> (80,823 sq mi), excluding the smaller surrounding islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unep_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-unep-46">[45]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/North_Channel_(Great_Britain_and_Ireland)" title="North Channel (Great Britain and Ireland)">North Channel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Irish_Sea" title="Irish Sea">Irish Sea</a>, <a href="/wiki/St_George%27s_Channel" title="St George's Channel">St George's Channel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Celtic_Sea" title="Celtic Sea">Celtic Sea</a> separate the island from the island of <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a> to its west.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup> The island is physically connected with continental Europe via the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Tunnel" title="Channel Tunnel">Channel Tunnel</a>, the longest undersea rail tunnel in the world, completed in 1993. The island is marked by low, rolling countryside in the east and south, while hills and mountains predominate in the western and northern regions. It is surrounded by over 1,000 smaller <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islands" title="Islands">islands</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islets" title="Islets">islets</a>. The greatest distance between two points is 968.0 km (<span class="frac nowrap">601<span class="visualhide"> </span><sup>1</sup>⁄<sub>2</sub></span> mi) (between <a href="/wiki/Land%27s_End" title="Land's End">Land's End</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_o%27_Groats" title="John o' Groats">John o' Groats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caithness" title="Caithness">Caithness</a>), 838 miles (1,349 km) by road.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/English_Channel" title="English Channel">English Channel</a> is thought to have been created between 450,000 and 180,000 years ago by two catastrophic <a href="/wiki/Glacial_lake_outburst_flood" title="Glacial lake outburst flood">glacial lake outburst floods</a> caused by the breaching of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weald-Artois_Anticline" title="Weald-Artois Anticline">Weald-Artois Anticline</a>, a ridge that held back a large <a href="/wiki/Proglacial_lake" title="Proglacial lake">proglacial lake</a>, now submerged under the North Sea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup> Around 10,000 years ago, during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Last_glacial_period#Named_local_glaciations" title="Last glacial period">Devensian glaciation</a> with its lower <a href="/wiki/Sea_level" title="Sea level">sea level</a>, Great Britain was not an island, but an upland region of continental northwestern Europe, lying partially underneath the Eurasian ice sheet. The sea level was about 120 metres (390 ft) lower than today, and the bed of the North Sea was dry and acted as a land bridge, now known as <a href="/wiki/Doggerland" title="Doggerland">Doggerland</a>, to the Continent. It is generally thought that as sea levels gradually rose after the end of the last glacial period of the current ice age, Doggerland became submerged beneath the North Sea, cutting off what was previously the British peninsula from the European mainland by around 6500 BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gaffney_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-gaffney-49">[48]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Britain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_Great_Britain" title="Geology of Great Britain">Geology of Great Britain</a></div>
<p>Great Britain has been subject to a variety of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plate_tectonic" title="Plate tectonic">plate tectonic</a> processes over a very extended period of time. Changing latitude and sea levels have been important factors in the nature of sedimentary sequences, whilst successive continental collisions have affected <a href="/wiki/Geological_structure_of_Great_Britain" title="Geological structure of Great Britain">its geological structure</a> with major faulting and folding being a legacy of each <a href="/wiki/Orogeny" title="Orogeny">orogeny</a> (mountain-building period), often associated with <a href="/wiki/Volcanism" title="Volcanism">volcanic</a> activity and the metamorphism of existing rock sequences. As a result of this eventful geological history, the island shows a rich variety of <a href="/wiki/Landscape" title="Landscape">landscapes</a>.
</p><p>The oldest rocks in Great Britain are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lewisian_gneiss" title="Lewisian gneiss">Lewisian gneisses</a>, metamorphic rocks found in the far north west of the island and in the <a href="/wiki/Hebrides" title="Hebrides">Hebrides</a> (with a few small outcrops elsewhere), which date from at least 2,700 Ma (Ma = million years ago). South of the gneisses are a complex mixture of rocks forming the North West <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Highlands" title="Scottish Highlands">Highlands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grampian" title="Grampian">Grampian</a> Highlands in Scotland. These are essentially the remains of folded <a href="/wiki/Sedimentary_rock" title="Sedimentary rock">sedimentary rocks</a> that were deposited between 1,000 Ma and 670 Ma over the gneiss on what was then the floor of the <a href="/wiki/Iapetus_Ocean" title="Iapetus Ocean">Iapetus Ocean</a>.
</p><p>At the present time the north of the island is rising as a result of the weight of Devensian ice being lifted. Southern and eastern Britain is sinking, generally estimated at 1 mm (1/25 inch) per year, with the London area sinking at double the speed partly due to the continuing <a href="/wiki/Compaction_(geology)" title="Compaction (geology)">compaction</a> of the recent clay deposits.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fauna">Fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Britain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Fauna_of_Great_Britain" title="Fauna of Great Britain">Fauna of Great Britain</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Robin,_Leighton_Moss_January_2009.jpg"><img alt="European robin on a branch facing left, tan plumage with orange face and throat" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Robin%2C_Leighton_Moss_January_2009.jpg/220px-Robin%2C_Leighton_Moss_January_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Robin%2C_Leighton_Moss_January_2009.jpg/330px-Robin%2C_Leighton_Moss_January_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Robin%2C_Leighton_Moss_January_2009.jpg/440px-Robin%2C_Leighton_Moss_January_2009.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Robin,_Leighton_Moss_January_2009.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/European_robin" title="European robin">robin</a> is popularly known as "Britain's favourite bird".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Animal <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">diversity</a> is modest, as a result of factors including the island's small land area, the relatively recent age of the habitats developed since the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Last_glacial_period" title="Last glacial period">last glacial period</a> and the island's physical separation from <a href="/wiki/Continental_Europe" title="Continental Europe">continental Europe</a>, and the effects of seasonal variability.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup> Great Britain also experienced early <a href="/wiki/Industrialisation" title="Industrialisation">industrialisation</a> and is subject to continuing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urbanisation" title="Urbanisation">urbanisation</a>, which have contributed towards the overall loss of species.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-animals_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-animals-52">[51]</a></sup> A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DEFRA" title="DEFRA">DEFRA</a> (Department for Environment, Food and Rural Affairs) study from 2006 suggested that 100 species have become extinct in the UK during the 20th century, about 100 times the <a href="/wiki/Background_extinction_rate" title="Background extinction rate">background extinction rate</a>. However, some species, such as the <a href="/wiki/Brown_rat" title="Brown rat">brown rat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Red_fox" title="Red fox">red fox</a>, and introduced <a href="/wiki/Eastern_gray_squirrel" title="Eastern gray squirrel">grey squirrel</a>, are well adapted to urban areas.
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rodents" title="Rodents">Rodents</a> make up 40% of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_mammals_of_Great_Britain" title="List of mammals of Great Britain">mammal species</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="data source? (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> These include <a href="/wiki/Squirrel" title="Squirrel">squirrels</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mice" title="Mice">mice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vole" title="Vole">voles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rat" title="Rat">rats</a> and the recently reintroduced <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_beaver" title="European beaver">European beaver</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-animals_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-animals-52">[51]</a></sup> There is also an abundance of <a href="/wiki/European_rabbit" title="European rabbit">European rabbit</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_hare" title="European hare">European hare</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shrews" title="Shrews">shrews</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_mole" title="European mole">European mole</a> and several species of <a href="/wiki/Bat" title="Bat">bat</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-animals_52-2"><a href="#cite_note-animals-52">[51]</a></sup> Carnivorous mammals include the <a href="/wiki/Red_fox" title="Red fox">red fox</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eurasian_badger" title="Eurasian badger">Eurasian badger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_otter" title="Eurasian otter">Eurasian otter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Weasel" title="Weasel">weasel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stoat" title="Stoat">stoat</a> and elusive <a href="/wiki/Scottish_wildcat" title="Scottish wildcat">Scottish wildcat</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-else_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-else-53">[52]</a></sup> Various species of <a href="/wiki/Pinniped" title="Pinniped">seal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Whale" title="Whale">whale</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dolphin" title="Dolphin">dolphin</a> are found on or around British shores and coastlines. The largest land-based wild animals today are <a href="/wiki/Deer" title="Deer">deer</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Red_deer" title="Red deer">red deer</a> is the largest species, with <a href="/wiki/Roe_deer" title="Roe deer">roe deer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fallow_deer" title="Fallow deer">fallow deer</a> also prominent; the latter was introduced by the <a href="/wiki/Normans" title="Normans">Normans</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-else_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-else-53">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sika_deer" title="Sika deer">Sika deer</a> and two more species of smaller deer, <a href="/wiki/Muntjac" title="Muntjac">muntjac</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chinese_water_deer" title="Chinese water deer">Chinese water deer</a>, have been introduced, muntjac becoming widespread in England and parts of Wales while Chinese water deer are restricted mainly to East Anglia. Habitat loss has affected many species. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_extinct_animals_of_Britain" title="List of extinct animals of Britain">Extinct large mammals</a> include the <a href="/wiki/Brown_bear" title="Brown bear">brown bear</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grey_wolf" title="Grey wolf">grey wolf</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wild_boar" title="Wild boar">wild boar</a>; the latter has had a limited reintroduction in recent times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-animals_52-3"><a href="#cite_note-animals-52">[51]</a></sup>
</p><p>There is a wealth of <a href="/wiki/List_of_birds_of_Great_Britain" title="List of birds of Great Britain">birdlife</a>, with 618 species recorded,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup> of which 258 breed on the island or remain during winter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup> Because of its mild winters for its latitude, Great Britain hosts important numbers of many wintering species, particularly <a href="/wiki/Wader" title="Wader">waders</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duck" title="Duck">ducks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goose" title="Goose">geese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Swan" title="Swan">swans</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup> Other well known bird species include the <a href="/wiki/Golden_eagle" title="Golden eagle">golden eagle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grey_heron" title="Grey heron">grey heron</a>, <a href="/wiki/Common_kingfisher" title="Common kingfisher">common kingfisher</a>, <a href="/wiki/Common_wood_pigeon" title="Common wood pigeon">common wood pigeon</a>, <a href="/wiki/House_sparrow" title="House sparrow">house sparrow</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_robin" title="European robin">European robin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grey_partridge" title="Grey partridge">grey partridge</a>, and various species of <a href="/wiki/Crow" title="Crow">crow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finch" title="Finch">finch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gull" title="Gull">gull</a>, <a href="/wiki/Auk" title="Auk">auk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grouse" title="Grouse">grouse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Owl" title="Owl">owl</a> and <a href="/wiki/Falcon" title="Falcon">falcon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-birds_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-birds-58">[57]</a></sup> There are six species of <a href="/wiki/List_of_reptiles_of_Great_Britain" title="List of reptiles of Great Britain">reptile</a> on the island; three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Snakes" title="Snakes">snakes</a> and three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lizards" title="Lizards">lizards</a> including the legless <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slowworm" title="Slowworm">slowworm</a>. One snake, the <a href="/wiki/Vipera_berus" title="Vipera berus">adder</a>, is venomous but rarely deadly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/List_of_amphibians_of_Great_Britain" title="List of amphibians of Great Britain">Amphibians</a> present are <a href="/wiki/Common_frog" title="Common frog">frogs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Common_toad" title="Common toad">toads</a> and <a href="/wiki/Smooth_newt" title="Smooth newt">newts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-animals_52-4"><a href="#cite_note-animals-52">[51]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora">Flora</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Britain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Flora">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_vascular_plants_of_Britain_and_Ireland" title="List of the vascular plants of Britain and Ireland">List of the vascular plants of Britain and Ireland</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Heather_(Highlands).jpg"><img alt="purple heather in meadow showing flower spikes" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="2468" decoding="async" height="205" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Heather_%28Highlands%29.jpg/220px-Heather_%28Highlands%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Heather_%28Highlands%29.jpg/330px-Heather_%28Highlands%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Heather_%28Highlands%29.jpg/440px-Heather_%28Highlands%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Heather_(Highlands).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Calluna_vulgaris" title="Calluna vulgaris">Heather</a> growing wild in the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Highlands" title="Scottish Highlands">Highlands</a> at <a href="/wiki/Dornoch" title="Dornoch">Dornoch</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>In a similar sense to fauna, and for similar reasons, the flora is impoverished compared to that of continental Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-floraa_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-floraa-60">[59]</a></sup> The flora comprises 3,354 <a href="/wiki/Vascular_plant" title="Vascular plant">vascular plant</a> species, of which 2,297 are native and 1,057 have been introduced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frodin_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-frodin-61">[60]</a></sup> The island has a wide variety of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trees_of_Britain_and_Ireland" title="Trees of Britain and Ireland">trees</a>, including native species of <a href="/wiki/Birch" title="Birch">birch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beech" title="Beech">beech</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fraxinus" title="Fraxinus">ash</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crataegus" title="Crataegus">hawthorn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elm" title="Elm">elm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oak" title="Oak">oak</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Common_yew" title="Common yew">yew</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pine" title="Pine">pine</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cherry_tree" title="Cherry tree">cherry</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apple_tree" title="Apple tree">apple</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tree_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-tree-62">[61]</a></sup> Other trees have been naturalised, introduced especially from other parts of Europe (particularly Norway) and North America. Introduced trees include several varieties of pine, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sweet_chestnut" title="Sweet chestnut">chestnut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Acer_platanoides" title="Acer platanoides">maple</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norway_spruce" title="Norway spruce">spruce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Acer_pseudoplatanus" title="Acer pseudoplatanus">sycamore</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fir" title="Fir">fir</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Cherry_plum" title="Cherry plum">cherry plum</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Pear" title="European Pear">pear trees</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tree_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-tree-62">[61]</a></sup> The tallest species are the <a href="/wiki/Douglas_fir" title="Douglas fir">Douglas firs</a>; two specimens have been recorded measuring 65 metres or 212 feet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Fortingall_Yew" title="Fortingall Yew">Fortingall Yew</a> in <a href="/wiki/Perthshire" title="Perthshire">Perthshire</a> is the oldest tree in Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup>
</p><p>There are at least 1,500 different species of <a href="/wiki/Wildflower" title="Wildflower">wildflower</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flowepow_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-flowepow-65">[64]</a></sup> Some 107 species are particularly rare or vulnerable and are protected by the <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_and_Countryside_Act_1981" title="Wildlife and Countryside Act 1981">Wildlife and Countryside Act 1981</a>. It is illegal to uproot any wildflowers without the landowner's permission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flowepow_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-flowepow-65">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup>
A vote in 2002 nominated various wildflowers to represent specific counties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup> These include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Common_poppy" title="Common poppy">red poppies</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Common_bluebell" title="Common bluebell">bluebells</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bellis_perennis" title="Bellis perennis">daisies</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Narcissus_(genus)" title="Narcissus (genus)">daffodils</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bog_rosemary" title="Bog rosemary">rosemary</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gorse" title="Gorse">gorse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iris_(plant)" title="Iris (plant)">iris</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ivy" title="Ivy">ivy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mentha" title="Mentha">mint</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orchid" title="Orchid">orchids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bramble" title="Bramble">brambles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thistle" title="Thistle">thistles</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buttercup" title="Buttercup">buttercups</a>, <a href="/wiki/Primula_vulgaris" title="Primula vulgaris">primrose</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thyme" title="Thyme">thyme</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tulips" title="Tulips">tulips</a>, <a href="/wiki/Viola_(plant)" title="Viola (plant)">violets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Primula_veris" title="Primula veris">cowslip</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Calluna_vulgaris" title="Calluna vulgaris">heather</a> and many more.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flora_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-flora-68">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup>
<br/>There are also many species of <a href="/wiki/Algae" title="Algae">algae</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mosses" title="Mosses">mosses</a> across the island.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fungi">Fungi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Britain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Fungi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are many species of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fungi" title="Fungi">fungi</a> including <a href="/wiki/Lichen" title="Lichen">lichen</a>-forming species, and the mycobiota is less poorly known than in many other parts of the world. The most recent checklist of Basidiomycota (bracket fungi, jelly fungi, mushrooms and toadstools, puffballs, rusts and smuts), published in 2005, accepts over 3600 species.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-legon_&amp;_henrici_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-legon_&amp;_henrici-72">[71]</a></sup> The most recent checklist of Ascomycota (cup fungi and their allies, including most lichen-forming fungi), published in 1985, accepts another 5100 species.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cannon,_hawskworth_&amp;_sherwood-pike_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-cannon,_hawskworth_&amp;_sherwood-pike-73">[72]</a></sup> These two lists did not include <a href="/wiki/Conidium" title="Conidium">conidial</a> fungi (fungi mostly with affinities in the Ascomycota but known only in their asexual state) or any of the other main fungal groups (Chytridiomycota, Glomeromycota and Zygomycota). The number of fungal species known very probably exceeds 10,000. There is widespread agreement among mycologists that many others are yet to be discovered.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Britain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demography_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Demography of the United Kingdom">Demography of the United Kingdom</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Settlements">Settlements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Great_Britain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Settlements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> is the capital of <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> and the whole of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, and is the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Government of the United Kingdom">United Kingdom's government</a>. <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cardiff" title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a> are the capitals of <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a>, respectively, and house their devolved governments.
</p>
